2006\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         present\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">\n        Primary and secondary education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_schools">\n        Public schools\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public schools">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Myrtle Beach is served by a single public school district.\n       <a href="/wiki/Horry_County_Schools" title="Horry County Schools">\n        Horry County Schools\n       </a>\n       educates around 40,000 students and is the third largest school district in South Carolina.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Private_Schools_and_Charter_Schools">\n        Private Schools and Charter Schools\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Private Schools and Charter Schools">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Below is a list of private schools and charter schools within the city of Myrtle Beach.\n      </p>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">\n       <ul>\n        <li>\n         St. Andrew\'s Catholic School\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Christian Academy of Myrtle Beach\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Carolina Bays Academy\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Chabad Academy\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Calvary Christian School\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Bridgewater Academy\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Cathedral Hall High School\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Christian Academy\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Life Christian Academy &amp; Child\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Socastee Montessori School\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Palmetto Academy of Learning and Success\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">\n        Higher education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Higher education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CCUBlantonPark.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/CCUBlantonPark.jpg/220px-CCUBlantonPark.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/CCUBlantonPark.jpg/330px-CCUBlantonPark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/CCUBlantonPark.jpg/440px-CCUBlantonPark.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CCUBlantonPark.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Carolina_University" title="Coastal Carolina University">\n          Coastal Carolina University\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The largest university in the Myrtle Beach area is\n       <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Carolina_University" title="Coastal Carolina University">\n        Coastal Carolina University\n       </a>\n       , a state-supported, liberal arts university located eight miles northwest of Myrtle Beach in neighboring\n       <a href="/wiki/Conway,_South_Carolina" title="Conway, South Carolina">\n        Conway\n       </a>\n       , with a satellite campus in Myrtle Beach. The university is a national sea-grant institution and owns part of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waties_Island" title="Waties Island">\n        Waties Island\n       </a>\n       , a 1,105-acre (4.47 km2) barrier island which serves as a natural laboratory. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Carolina_Chanticleers" title="Coastal Carolina Chanticleers">\n        Coastal Carolina Chanticleers\n       </a>\n       compete in\n       <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">\n        NCAA Division I\n       </a>\n       as a member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun_Belt_Conference" title="Sun Belt Conference">\n        Sun Belt Conference\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Carolina_Chanticleers_football" title="Coastal Carolina Chanticleers football">\n        football\n       </a>\n       team competes in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="NCAA Football Bowl Subdivision">\n        NCAA Football Bowl Subdivision\n       </a>\n       or FBS. The football team plays at\n       <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Stadium" title="Brooks Stadium">\n        Brooks Stadium\n       </a>\n       , which is notable for its teal artificial turf.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Myrtle Beach metro area has the following college and post-secondary schools:\n      </p>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">\n       <ul>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Golf_Academy_of_America" title="Golf Academy of America">\n          Golf Academy of America\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         Palmetto School of Career Development \xe2\x80\x93 Myrtle Beach Campus\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Horry-Georgetown_Technical_College" title="Horry-Georgetown Technical College">\n          Horry-Georgetown Technical College\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/ITT_Technical_Institute" title="ITT Technical Institute">\n          ITT Technical Institute\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Miller-Motte_Technical_College" title="Miller-Motte Technical College">\n          Miller-Motte Technical College\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <a href="/wiki/Webster_University" title="Webster University">\n          Webster University\n         </a>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 Myrtle Beach Campus\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <br/>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">\n        Media\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span in South Carolina\n             </a>\n            </dd>\n           </dl>\n          </div>\n         </td>\n        </tr>\n       </table>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">\n        Newspapers\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Newspapers">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Sun_News" title="The Sun News">\n         The Sun News\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       is the largest daily paper published along the Grand Strand, with a readership base extending from\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_South_Carolina" title="Georgetown, South Carolina">\n        Georgetown, South Carolina\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Beach,_North_Carolina" title="Sunset Beach, North Carolina">\n        Sunset Beach, North Carolina\n       </a>\n       . The paper has been in existence since the 1930s and was formerly published by\n       <a href="/wiki/Knight_Ridder" title="Knight Ridder">\n        Knight Ridder\n       </a>\n       before that company was bought by\n       <a href="/wiki/The_McClatchy_Company" title="The McClatchy Company">\n        The McClatchy Company\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Myrtle Beach is also served by\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Myrtle_Beach_Herald" title="The Myrtle Beach Herald">\n         The Myrtle Beach Herald\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , a weekly newspaper that is part of the Waccamaw Publishers group. It is locally owned by Steve and Cheryl Robertson.\n       <i>\n        The Herald\n       </i>\n       also produces a newspaper targeted at tourists called\n       <i>\n        Visit!\n       </i>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">\n        Infrastructure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">\n        Air\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Air">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="754" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg/220px-Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg/330px-Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg/440px-Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Myr-marketcommon-commerce.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/The_Market_Common" title="The Market Common">\n          The Market Common\n         </a>\n         was once the location of Myrtle Beach AFB.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach_International_Airport" title="Myrtle Beach International Airport">\n         Myrtle Beach International Airport\n        </a>\n        (IATA: MYR/FAA LID: MYR), is a county-owned public-use airport located three nautical miles (5.6\xc2\xa0km) southwest of the central business district of Myrtle Beach, in Horry County, South Carolina, United States. (\n        <a class="external text" href="http://www.gcr1.com/5010web/airport.cfm?Site=MYR" rel="nofollow">\n         MYR\n        </a>\n        ) It was formerly known as Myrtle Beach Jetport (1974\xe2\x80\x931989) and is located on site of the former Myrtle Beach Air Force Base.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The General Aviation Terminal www.beachaviationservices.com (ICAO: KMYR/FAA LID:MYR), is a part of the Myrtle Beach International Airport however, the terminal itself is located on the opposite side of the airfield from the commercial terminal side of the airport on Airdrome Street accessed by Phyllis Boulevard inside\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Market_Common" title="The Market Common">\n         The Market Common\n        </a>\n        . This new 11,500 square foot terminal was opened on May 21, 2010, built to modernize operations and accommodate the growing needs of the terminal. The new terminal replaces a building that was previously used as Base Operations when the Myrtle Beach Air Force Base was active.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Executive Helicopters is within the Myrtle Beach International Airport as well. It is located on the eastern side of the airport with access from Kings Highway. Executive Helicopters is a private helicopter facility that provides tour services in the Myrtle Beach and surrounding areas.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        they also provide the majority of maintenance for General Aviation. In addition; Myrtle Air Service a division of Kingman Aircraft Kingman, AZ operate a maintenance facility on site providing maintenance for mid sized jets. Military operations are also ongoing supporting USMC, USN, USAF, US Army and Coast Guard.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Grand_Strand_Airport" title="Grand Strand Airport">\n         Grand Strand Airport\n        </a>\n        (IATA: CRE, ICAO: KCRE, FAA LID: CRE), is a county-owned (Horry County), public-use airport located one nautical mile (1.85\xc2\xa0km) northwest of the central business district of North Myrtle Beach, in Horry County, South Carolina, United States.\n        <a href="/wiki/Grand_Strand_Airport" title="Grand Strand Airport">\n         Grand Strand Airport\n        </a>\n        is a single-terminal airport, serving primarily banner planes and small aircraft. Ramp 66 is the Fixed-Base Operator (FBO) for the Grand Strand Airport providing services such as fuel, oxygen, hangar service, maintenance, and inspections.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Conway Airport (IATA: HYW, ICAO: KHYW, LID: HYW) is an Horry County owned airport that services the General Aviation Community of Horry County and Conway, SC. This airport has under gone major improvements in 2016-17 with the addition of LED lighting on the runway and taxiways.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">\n        Rail\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Rail">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Waccamaw_Coast_Line_Railroad" title="Waccamaw Coast Line Railroad">\n        Waccamaw Coast Line Railroad\n       </a>\n       is a 14.1-mile (22.7\xc2\xa0km)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short-line_railroad" title="Short-line railroad">\n        short-line railroad\n       </a>\n       division of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Annapolis_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Annapolis Railroad">\n        Baltimore and Annapolis Railroad\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       extending from a connection with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Southern_Railroad" title="Carolina Southern Railroad">\n        Carolina Southern Railroad\n       </a>\n       , another division of that company, at Conway to Myrtle Beach. The line was opened in 1900 by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Conway_Coast_and_Western_Railroad" title="Conway Coast and Western Railroad">\n        Conway Coast and Western Railroad\n       </a>\n       , a predecessor of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Line_Railroad" title="Atlantic Coast Line Railroad">\n        Atlantic Coast Line Railroad\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Seaboard_System_Railroad" title="Seaboard System Railroad">\n        Seaboard System Railroad\n       </a>\n       sold the line to\n       <a href="/wiki/Horry_County,_South_Carolina" title="Horry County, South Carolina">\n        Horry County\n       </a>\n       in November 1984, and it was operated by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horry_County_Railway" title="Horry County Railway">\n        Horry County Railway\n       </a>\n       until October 1987, when the WCLR took over.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shortline_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-shortline-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Carolina Southern Railroad acquired the WCLR in September 1995, and since then it has been a division of the Baltimore and Annapolis Railroad.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The line is owned by Horry County, but was leased in 2000 to the Carolina Southern Railroad.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Southern_Railroad" title="Carolina Southern Railroad">\n        Carolina Southern Railroad\n       </a>\n       is a short line rail operator running on less than 100 miles (160\xc2\xa0km) of rail at a maximum speed of 10\xc2\xa0mph (16\xc2\xa0km/h). It transports mostly freight brought to it from national rail operators. The company makes one scheduled delivery per month into the City of Myrtle Beach.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is located off of Main Street in Conway, South Carolina and is one of the few remaining train depots in South Carolina. It has been Painstakingly restored to its former glory and the Carolina Southern Railroad has become one of the frequent destinations for freight services as well as passenger cars and observational locomotives. The railroad was originally erected in late 1886 and the first train steamed into the Conway Depot in December 1887. The Carolina Southern Railroad stands as a permanent landmark in Southern History. Carolina Southern Railroad is a member of the Carolina Rails system with connections that run from\n       <a href="/wiki/Whiteville,_North_Carolina" title="Whiteville, North Carolina">\n        Whiteville, North Carolina\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mullins,_South_Carolina" title="Mullins, South Carolina">\n        Mullins, South Carolina\n       </a>\n       and also from\n       <a href="/wiki/Chadbourn,_North_Carolina" title="Chadbourn, North Carolina">\n        Chadbourn, North Carolina\n       </a>\n       to Conway. Carolina Southern railroad is also responsible for operation of the Waccamaw Coast Line Railroad, which is a railway that runs from Conway to Myrtle Beach. On August 30, 2011, Carolina Southern Railroad voluntary shut down because several bridges along the rail were overdue for maintenance. The shutdown caused Carolina Southern Railroad to lay off nearly all of its employees. On May 24, 2012, the Federal Railroad Administration (FRA) commenced a bridge inspection on the CSR and the Waccamaw Coastline Railroad (the Horry County portion of rail). Fifty-two of 187 bridges were inspected and seven had critical defects. On May 26, 2011, the CSR voluntarily ceased operation, so that they could bring in a certified bridge engineer to inspect the seven critical bridges and prepare a plan for their repairs. Based on the engineer\xe2\x80\x99s recommendations, CSR made the necessary repairs on the bridges and CSR resumed operations August 8, 2011. The FRA returned to inspect the bridges and made a recommendation that CSR cease operations until all bridge repairs were completed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horry_County_South_Carolina_and_Carolina_Southern_Railroad_Infrastructure_Project_2012_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Horry_County_South_Carolina_and_Carolina_Southern_Railroad_Infrastructure_Project_2012-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are currently efforts to bring the railroad back online.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carolina_Southern_Railroad_Revitalization_Project-Cost_Estimate_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carolina_Southern_Railroad_Revitalization_Project-Cost_Estimate-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carolina_Southern_Railroad_Revitalization_Project-Cost_Estimate_59-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Carolina_Southern_Railroad_Revitalization_Project-Cost_Estimate-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2015, railroad operator RJ Corman acquired the former CSR line and plans to re-open freight service in early 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">\n        Roads\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Roads">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg/220px-CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg/330px-CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2c/CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg/440px-CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CarolinaBaysPkwy22.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Highway_31" title="South Carolina Highway 31">\n          SC 31\n         </a>\n         serves as a by-pass for a majority of the Grand Strand\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/US_17.svg/20px-US_17.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/US_17.svg/30px-US_17.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/US_17.svg/40px-US_17.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>\n        <span class="nowrap">\n         <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_17_in_South_Carolina" title="U.S. Route 17 in South Carolina">\n          US\xc2\xa017\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="750" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/US_501.svg/25px-US_501.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/US_501.svg/38px-US_501.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/US_501.svg/50px-US_501.svg.png 2x" width="25"/>\n        <span class="nowrap">\n         <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_501_in_South_Carolina" title="U.S. Route 501 in South Carolina">\n          US\xc2\xa0501\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="750" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/South_Carolina_31.svg/25px-South_Carolina_31.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/South_Carolina_31.svg/38px-South_Carolina_31.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/South_Carolina_31.svg/50px-South_Carolina_31.svg.png 2x" width="25"/>\n        <span class="nowrap">\n         <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Highway_31" title="South Carolina Highway 31">\n          SC\xc2\xa031\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <img alt="" data-file-height="301" data-file-width="601" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Business_plate.svg/20px-Business_plate.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Business_plate.svg/30px-Business_plate.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Business_plate.svg/40px-Business_plate.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>\n        <br/>\n        <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Farrow_Parkway" title="Farrow Parkway">\n         Farrow Parkway\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Highway_73" title="South Carolina Highway 73">\n         Ocean Boulevard\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Harrelson_Boulevard" title="Harrelson Boulevard">\n         Harrelson Boulevard\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Robert_Grissom_Parkway" title="Robert Grissom Parkway">\n         Grissom Parkway\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_73" title="Interstate 73">\n         Interstate 73 (future)\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_74" title="Interstate 74">\n         Interstate 74 (future)\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Within the last decade, new roads have been created to ease congestion caused by the yearly influx of visitors. Most of these roads follow the Metro Loop Road Plan\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       , organized in 1997 to improve the traffic flow of Myrtle Beach. Some of the roads included have either been funded through\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road_Improvement_Development_Effort" title="Road Improvement Development Effort">\n        Road Improvement Development Effort\n       </a>\n       (RIDE I) funding or through the City of Myrtle Beach.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       RIDE II plans include the third phase of\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Highway_31" title="South Carolina Highway 31">\n        S.C. Highway 31\n       </a>\n       , a graded separation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Farrow_Parkway" title="Farrow Parkway">\n        Farrow Parkway\n       </a>\n       and US 17 Bypass at the back gate of the former Air Force base, and many other projects. The county is currently debating where to allocate the $400 million generated through a proposed 1-cent sales tax\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       . Other road projects in Horry County, including some in\n       <a href="/wiki/Aynor,_South_Carolina" title="Aynor, South Carolina">\n        Aynor\n       </a>\n       and Conway, will be included when voted upon.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Plans exist for Myrtle Beach to be eventually served by two interstates,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_73" title="Interstate 73">\n        Interstate 73\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_74" title="Interstate 74">\n        Interstate 74\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Edge_Parkway" title="Robert Edge Parkway">\n        Robert Edge Parkway\n       </a>\n       will connect I-74 to downtown\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina" title="North Myrtle Beach, South Carolina">\n        North Myrtle Beach\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_transit">\n        Mass transit\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Mass transit">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Myrtle Beach is served by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Coast_RTA" title="Coast RTA">\n        Coast RTA\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pee_Dee_Regional_Transportation_Authority" title="Pee Dee Regional Transportation Authority">\n        Pee Dee Regional Transportation Authority\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">\n        Healthcare\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Healthcare">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Grand Strand Regional Medical Center is a 219-bed acute care hospital serving residents and visitors of Horry and surrounding counties. The hospital offers the only cardiac surgery program in the area and is also a designated trauma center. Over 250 physicians serve at the facility.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">\n        Sister cities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n
